You can't make something dead healthy. Dead things are dry and lack moisture, think of dried rose petals. You can't make them alive and healthy again, you can't resurrect hair, so essentially you're just doing what you can to make it look and feel healthy and alive, like reconstituting dried fruit in water. You do that with oil, which is why your own scalp coats hair with oil and why brushing your hair to distribute that natural oil before washing hair is so important.<br /><br />So here's what I do. I use whatever product makes my hair feel and look the best (isn't that what we care about anyway?) and once a week I wash my hair with a clarifying shampoo to remove all of the build up and cones that have sat on top making it look smooth, and after it dries I apply a mixture of 100% natural oils, jojoba, coconut, and Argan with vitamin E added.   776. This is not pure argan oil, it's an argan oil serum, which means it has added silicone. I really like this treatment, it conditions, eliminates frizz, adds shine and provides thermal protection (thanks to the silicone). I apply about a nickel size dollop to clean, damp hair (mine is below shoulder length) concentrating first on the ends and then working my way up, but avoiding the roots. Then I take whatever's left on my hands and smooth the top. Next I apply my regular styling products. This treatment produces similar results to Moroccan Oil or Macadamia Professional because all three are essentially the same thing. However, if you want pure organic argan oil, it is available on Amazon for a very decent price. If you use pure argan oil, apply it to damp hair in the same manner as I have described. Give it a few minutes to soak in before you use styling products. Pure argan oil is NOT a heat protectant so if you're planning on using heated styling tools, another product that has silicone is required. I also use pure argan oil on my hair but I use it at night on dry hair and then shampoo in the morning. Or you can use it mixed in with any conditioning mask. It works best with heat, either a hot towel or a heat cap. I use argan oil both ways but for styling I prefer Agadir, Moroccanoil or Macadamia Professional treatments. I do think they condition my hair and I expect it to look better and better over time. Pure argan oil does nothing for frizz (I know, I live in Florida, the frizz capital of the Western Hemisphere) so one of these treatments is absolutely essential for me. But if you want pure argan oil, do your research and you'll find good buys on Amazon. The last time I purchased some I paid $10 for 4 ounces, which is a huge bottle. However, I will continue to use one of these argan or macadamia oil treatments because I use a curling iron several times a week and I need the thermal protection.
